<div id="review_943106903" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/943106903" />
    <a title="Marc *Dark Reader of the Woods*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29163734-marc-dark-reader-of-the-woods"><img alt="Marc *Dark Reader of the Woods*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602607922p2/29163734.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/943106903?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marc *Dark Reader of the Woods*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marc *Dark Reader of the Woods*" href="/user/show/29163734-marc-dark-reader-of-the-woods">Marc *Dark Reader of the Woods*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552134644" href="/book/show/833424.Reaper_Man">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29163734-marc-dark-reader-of-the-woods?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer943106903" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2652380085852396380">Oddly, I think that I never read this one until now. Is it possible that I might have skipped a Discworld book in my youth? I suppose so because no part of it rung any memory bells. Imagine, getting to read a Discworld book for the first time ever! Too bad it wasn't a better one...<br/><br/>Don't get me wrong, there was plenty to like about this book. Death is always a hoot. (The personification, that is, not the event). The arc between Bill Door and Miss Flitworth was the best sequence, at times philosop</span>
  <span id="freeText2652380085852396380" style="display:none">Oddly, I think that I never read this one until now. Is it possible that I might have skipped a Discworld book in my youth? I suppose so because no part of it rung any memory bells. Imagine, getting to read a Discworld book for the first time ever! Too bad it wasn't a better one...<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, there was plenty to like about this book. Death is always a hoot. (The personification, that is, not the event). The arc between Bill Door and Miss Flitworth was the best sequence, at times philosophical and heartfelt. Some beloved series characters see their genesis here, such as Reg Shoe, the zombie activist for dead rights, a hilarious character concept. I was pleased to see the origin of the Death of Rats, since I remembered him from later books and was confused by a statement in an earlier book during my current series re-read that there is only one Death for all living things. There were plenty of chuckle-to-LOL moments to be had. The plot flowed well, which I still appreciate after some instances where it notably did not in some earlier Discworld books. The faculty of Unseen University which, after many turnovers in the series to date, persisted from the prior book and those characters were nicely fleshed out. And as for Mrs. Cake... <br /><br />Where the book fell flat was in the entire arc taking place in Ankh-Morpork. It started well, made great use of characters, but I started to feel uncomfortable once shopping carts started appearing, and the final form of the "city predator", an organic <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ shopping mall, lost me. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34510.Moving_Pictures__Discworld___10__Industrial_Revolution___1_" title="Moving Pictures (Discworld, #10; Industrial Revolution, #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Moving Pictures</a> I found that the concept of Hollywood simply didn't mesh thematically with the Discworld, and the same thing happened here. A modern innovation/banality is given a fantasy form, and <i>it just doesn't work</i>. It also failed to intersect meaningfully with the main Death story, despite that it was driven by the cosmic fallout from that other storyline. This is especially unfortunate because the Ankh-Morpork events take up the bulk of the pages. It feels as though Pratchett had a story to tell about Death that simply didn't yield enough content for a full novel, so he had to tack on another story. That other story excelled in characters, but the grand concept was just too un-Disc-like for my taste. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="2652380085852396380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1701290373" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1701290373" />
    <a title="YouKneeK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek"><img alt="YouKneeK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386369592p2/25923230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1701290373?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YouKneeK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YouKneeK" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek">YouKneeK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1701290373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7817717074445477680"><i>Reaper Man</i> is the second book in the <i>Death</i> subseries of the <i>Discworld</i> universe. In this book, Death essentially gets fired for having developed too much of an individual personality. Until somebody is found to replace him, people aren’t dying properly. There are two main characters in the story, each with separate but related storylines. Death is one of them, and the other is a 130-year-old wizard named Windle Poons. Poons fails to die properly without Death on the job and thus becomes undead.<br/><br/>Wi</span>
  <span id="freeText7817717074445477680" style="display:none"><i>Reaper Man</i> is the second book in the <i>Death</i> subseries of the <i>Discworld</i> universe. In this book, Death essentially gets fired for having developed too much of an individual personality. Until somebody is found to replace him, people aren’t dying properly. There are two main characters in the story, each with separate but related storylines. Death is one of them, and the other is a 130-year-old wizard named Windle Poons. Poons fails to die properly without Death on the job and thus becomes undead.<br /><br />Windle Poons himself was a fun character, but his part of the story wasn’t all that interesting to me. I was more interested in what would happen with the Death character, and I’d been looking forward to reading more about him. However, Death really didn’t show up that much during the first half of the book and his story was on the skimpy side. I also thought the story seemed pretty disjointed, even for a <i>Discworld</i> book. <br /><br />On the other hand, Pratchett was as witty as usual and there were some very funny parts. So I enjoyed the humor, but was less enamored of the story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7817717074445477680" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rVORb52kRcjVK4W74WN/lzsIBdNTYJuq+WbYVW2NseqXdfi9JvqMoHIAMdoWlnVI7VfiG53tFc2iGJ7koM5DcA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5gPKRopWIShDZ4Fb8YkBAg4FnjcvFcDFjz4tZfKCcr/cJaOUMQjoQORMNToGfAvd2Fp5/+GYTqLUQGvUP8GAJQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12748022047595977341">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br/><br/>Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, i</span>
  <span id="freeText12748022047595977341" style="display:none">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <i>The Color of Magic</i>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <i>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</i>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <i>Good Omens</i>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <i>Nation</i>. Terry published <i>Snuff</i> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire (OBE) “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from the University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, the University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
